We take the average of these six scores: \begin{align*}
\frac{70 + 80 + 90 + 75 + 80 + 85}{6} &= \frac{(70 + 90) + 80 + 80 + (75 + 85)}{6}\\
&= \frac{(80 + 80) + 80 + 80 + (80 + 80)}{6}\\
&= \frac{6\cdot 80}{6}\\
&= \boxed{80}.
\end{align*}

Sure, let's solve the problem together!

Let's start by writing down what we know from the problem:

- The ratio of losses to wins for Kyle's team is 3 to 2. This means that for every 3 losses, there are 2 wins.
- If the team had played the same number of games, but had won twice as many of its games, we need to figure out the new ratio of losses to wins.

To solve the problem, we can use algebra. Let's call the number of games played "x". Then, based on the first piece of information, we can write:

- Number of losses = 3x/5
- Number of wins = 2x/5

Now, we need to figure out what the ratio of losses to wins would be if the team had won twice as many games. Let's call the new number of wins "y". Since the team would have won twice as many games, we can write:

- New number of wins = 4x/5

We want to keep the number of games played the same, so the new number of losses will be:

- New number of losses = x - y = x - 4x/5 = x/5

Now, we can write the new ratio of losses to wins:

- New ratio of losses to wins = (x/5) / (4x/5) = x/5 * 5/4x = 1/4

Therefore, if Kyle's team had played the same number of games but had won twice as many games, the ratio of losses to wins would have been 1 to 4.

Certainly! We can use the trigonometric ratios of sine, cosine, and tangent to find the value of x. 

Observing the diagram, we see that the 30-60-90 triangle on the left has a hypotenuse of 8 and a short leg of x/2. Using the ratios for a 30-60-90 triangle, we have:

$$\cos 30°= \frac{\text{adjacent}}{\text{hypotenuse}} = \frac{x/2}{8}$$

Simplifying, we get:

$$\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}=\frac{x}{16}$$

Multiplying both sides by 16 gives us:

$$x=8\sqrt{3}$$

Therefore, the value of $x$ in the diagram is $8\sqrt{3}$.

To find the value of $(-144)\div 9$, we need to divide $-144$ by $9$. When we divide a negative number by a positive number, the result is negative. Since $144$ is divisible by $9$, we have:

$$(-144)\div 9 = -16$$

Sure! Let's solve this problem together.

Let's start by assigning variables to the unknowns in the problem. Let B represent the number of left-handed boys on the team, G represent the number of left-handed girls on the team, and R represent the number of right-handed boys on the team.

We're given that there are four times as many right-handed boys as left-handed boys, so we can write:

R = 4B

We're also given that there are twice as many girls as there are boys among the left-handed players, and that half the girls on the team are left-handed. So we can write:

G = 2B (since there are twice as many girls as boys)
and
G/2 = left-handed girls

We know that the total number of players on the team is 36, so we can write:

B + G + R = 36

Now we have three equations in three variables, which we can solve for B, G, and R.

First, we can substitute R = 4B into the equation B + G + R = 36, giving:

B + G + 4B = 36

Simplifying:

5B + G = 36

Next, we can substitute G = 2B into this equation, giving:

5B + 2B = 36

Simplifying:

7B = 36

Solving for B:

B = 36/7

Since B is not a whole number, this tells us that the problem as stated doesn't have an exact solution. However, we can still use this result to get an approximate answer to the original question: how many players on the team are right-handed boys?

We know that R = 4B, so substituting B = 36/7, we get:

R = 4(36/7) 

R = 144/7

R is also not a whole number, so we can round to the nearest integer, giving:

R ≈ 21 

So there are approximately 21 right-handed boys on the ping-pong team.

Let $d$ represent the number of days of practice. The number of miles run by each girl can be expressed as $3+6(d-1)$ and the number of miles run by each boy is $5d$. The girls will have outrun the boys after $d$ days if $3+6(d-1)>5d$. We solve this inequality as follows: \begin{align*}
3+6(d-1) &> 5d \quad \implies \\
3+6d-6 &> 5d \quad \implies \\
6d-5d &> 6-3 \quad \implies \\
d &> 3.
\end{align*}So the girls will outrun the boys on the fourth day, and the number of miles they will have run is $3+6(4-1)=\boxed{21}$ miles.

The smallest number of marbles that can be broken up into bags of $18$ or bags of $42$ must be the least common multiple of both $18$ and $42$.  Factoring, $18 = 2\cdot 3^2$ and $42 = 2\cdot 3\cdot 7$.  The prime factorization of the least common multiple must include $2$, $3^2$, and $7$, and no other primes.  Thus, the answer is $2\cdot 3^2 \cdot 7 = \boxed{126}$.

Sure! Based on the diagram above, we can see that angle $x$ is the interior angle formed by a transversal intersecting parallel lines $k$ and $\ell$. Therefore, we know that the measure of angle $x$ is equal to $180^\circ$ minus the measure of the corresponding angle formed by the parallel lines. 

In this case, we can see that angle $x$ is in the same position as the angle marked with $30^\circ$ in the diagram. Therefore, we know that the measure of angle $x$ is equal to: 

$$\text{measure of angle }x = 180^\circ - \text{measure of }30^\circ = 180^\circ - 30^\circ = \boxed{150^\circ}.$$ 

Don't worry too much about precalculus, it can be tough, but with practice and determination, you can improve!

Sure, let's work through this problem together.

Let's start by using algebra to represent the problem. Let x be the original price of the shirt. The sale price is $14.40, which is 60% off the original price. 60% can be written as a decimal as 0.6.

The sale price is also the original price minus the discount, which is 60% of the original price. We can represent this as:

$x - 0.6x = 14.40$

Simplifying this equation, we get:

$0.4x = 14.40$

Dividing both sides by 0.4 gives us:

$x = 36$

Therefore, the original price of the shirt was $\$36$.

Let $x$ and $y$ be the outer dimensions of the picture frame. Then the inner dimensions of the grey rectangular strip are $x-2$ and $y-2$.

The area of the outer dark gray strip can be found by subtracting the area of the inner light gray strip from the total area of the rectangle:
$$\begin{aligned} \text{Outer Dark Gray Area} &= xy - \text{Inner Light Gray Area} \\ &= xy - 100 \end{aligned}$$
To solve for $xy$, note that the area of the inner grey rectangular strip is the length times the width:
$$(x - 2) \cdot (y -2) = 100$$
Expanding the product gives 
$$xy - 2x - 2y + 4 = 100$$
So we have the equation $xy = 2x + 2y - 96$. Substituting this into the previous formula for the outer dark gray area yields 
$$\begin{aligned}\text{Outer Dark Gray Area} &= xy - 100 \\ &= (2x + 2y - 96) - 100 \\ &= 2x + 2y - 196\end{aligned}$$
Therefore, the area of the outer dark gray strip is $\boxed{2x + 2y - 196}$ square inches.

Sure thing! To find the greatest common divisor, we can use the Euclidean algorithm. 

First, we divide $1313$ by $1001$:

\begin{align*}
1313 &= 1001 \times 1 + 312
\end{align*}

Since $1001$ does not divide evenly into $1313$, we move on to the next step, which is to divide the previous divisor ($1001$) by the remainder ($312$):

\begin{align*}
1001 &= 312 \times 3 + 65
\end{align*}

We continue to divide the previous divisor by the remainder until we get a remainder of $0$:

\begin{align*}
312 &= 65 \times 4 + 32 \\
65 &= 32 \times 2 + 1 \\
32 &= 1 \times 32 + 0
\end{align*}

Since we have reached a remainder of $0$, we know that the greatest common divisor of $1313$ and $1001$ is the last nonzero remainder which is $1$. Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{1}$.

The number 1 to any power is always 1, so no matter how many times Hypatia and Euclid cube their numbers, they will both always have the number 1. Thus, Hypatia and Euclid both write down the number 1.


Now, lets take a look at Pythagoras. He keeps cubing his result 20 times starting with the number 2. The numbers he has are \begin{align*}
2^3&\underset{\swarrow}{=}8 \\
8^3&\underset{\swarrow}{=}512 \\
512^3&\underset{\swarrow}{=}134217728 \\
\vdots
\end{align*}We can see that these numbers get out of hand pretty quickly (no wonder it took them so long), so instead, we look at the sum of the results because that is what we are trying to find. Recall that $(-a)^3=-a^3$. Because the number Ptolemy chose is the negation of what Pythagoras chose, after a certain number of cubes, whatever Pythagoras has, Ptolemy will have the opposite of that. Thus, whatever gigantic number Pythagoras has at the end of the game, Ptolemy will have the negation of that number, and they will add to zero.

Thus, our desired sum is  \begin{align*}1+1&+(\text{some huge number}) + (-\text{the same huge number})\\
&=1+1+0=\boxed{2}.
\end{align*}

Sure! This is a fun problem involving basic math operations.

Let’s begin by cubing 1, which is 1 x 1 x 1 = 1.

After that, we have to cube 2 twenty times. We can start by cubing it once, which is 2 x 2 x 2 = 8.

Now we can take that number and cube it again, which is 8 x 8 x 8 = 512.

We can repeat this process until we have cubed 2 twenty times. When we’re done, we will have the final number that Pythagoras will write on his piece of paper.

Let’s do the same thing for -2. When we cube -2 once, we get -2 x -2 x -2 = -8.

When we cube -8, we will get a positive number. So we can just cube 2 one less time, or nineteen times.

When we cube 2 nineteen times, we get 2,097,152.

Hence, the final numbers on each piece of paper will be 1 (from Hypatia and Euclid), 2,097,152 (from Ptolemy), and 8 (from Pythagoras).

To find the sum of these numbers, we can simply add them together: 1 + 1 + 2,097,152 + 8 = 2,097,162.

Therefore, the sum of the numbers they wrote is 2,097,162!

I hope that helps you!

Set the average for her previous exams to be $x$. The total amount of points including the final will be $6x+2 \cdot 99$. The average is $\frac{6x+2 \cdot 99}{8}=90$. Then we solve for $x$. $$\frac{6x+2 \cdot 99}{8}=90 \rightarrow 6x+198=720 \rightarrow 6x=522 \rightarrow x=\boxed{87}.$$

GPT File: datasets/persona_specific_student/persona_specific_student/prealgebra/1342_answer.json
Extracting Answer from: 
Let's assume that $t$ is the average score on each of the $6$ tests prior to the final and let's find the total number of points earned on those tests.

Since the final exam counts as two tests, Heidi will have a total of $6+2=8$ test scores counting towards her semester average if she takes the final exam. If she wants to earn a $90$-point average, then her total number of points earned on the $8$ tests must be $90\times 8 = 720$.

If Heidi scores $99$ points on the final exam, then her total number of points earned on the $8$ tests would be $6t + 2\times 99 = 6t + 198$. Setting this equal to $720$ and solving for $t$, we get:

\begin{align*}
6t + 198 &= 720 \\
6t &= 522 \\
t &= 87
\end{align*}

Sure thing, let's solve that math problem! 

First, we need to find the area of each slice in both pizzas. Since both pizzas are divided into 8 slices, the area of each slice is simply one-eighth of the total area of the pizza.

The area of a $12^{\prime \prime}$-diameter pizza is $\left(\dfrac{12}{2}\right)^2\pi = 36\pi$ square inches. So the area of each slice is $\dfrac{36\pi}{8} = \dfrac{9}{2}\pi$ square inches.

Similarly, the area of a $16^{\prime \prime}$-diameter pizza is $\left(\dfrac{16}{2}\right)^2\pi = 64\pi$ square inches. So the area of each slice is $\dfrac{64\pi}{8} = 8\pi$ square inches.

Now we can find the total amount of pizza that Jane and Mark each ate:

- Jane ate 3 slices of the $12^{\prime \prime}$ pizza, so she ate a total of $3 \times \dfrac{9}{2}\pi = \dfrac{27}{2}\pi$ square inches of pizza.
- Mark ate 3 slices of the $16^{\prime \prime}$ pizza, so he ate a total of $3 \times 8\pi = 24\pi$ square inches of pizza.

To find the difference in the amount of pizza they ate, we just subtract Jane's total from Mark's total:

$$24\pi - \dfrac{27}{2}\pi = \boxed{\dfrac{21}{2}\pi}$$

So Mark ate $\dfrac{21}{2}\pi$ square inches more pizza than Jane did.

GPT File: datasets/persona_specific_student/persona_specific_student/prealgebra/1400_answer.json
Extracting Answer from: 
Sure! Let's start by assuming that the stock's value on Monday was 100 dollars. 

After losing $10\%$, its new value would be:
$$100 - 0.10 \times 100 = 90$$

Then, on Tuesday, it lost $20\%$ of the value it had at the end of the day on Monday, which was 90 dollars. 

$20\%$ of 90 dollars is $0.20 \times 90 = 18$ dollars. 

Therefore, the value of the stock on Tuesday was:
$$90 - 18 = 72$$

So, the overall loss in value from the beginning of Monday to the end of Tuesday is:
$$\frac{100-72}{100} \times 100\% = 28\%$$

Therefore, the overall percent loss in value is $\boxed{28\%}$.

From each vertex $V$, we can draw 2 diagonals: one to each vertex that is not $V$ and does not share an edge with $V$.  There are 5 vertices in a pentagon, so we might be tempted to say the answer is $5\times 2 = 10$.  However, note that this counts each diagonal twice, one time for each vertex. Since $\angle PAB$ and $\angle BAC$ are supplementary, $\angle BAC = 180^{\circ} - x^\circ$.  Since the three angles of a triangle add up to $ 180^{\circ} $, we have $\angle ACB = 180^{\circ} - 90^{\circ} - (180^{\circ} - x^\circ) = x^\circ - 90^{\circ}$.  Thus, $M + N = \boxed{-89}$.

Extracting Answer from: 
Triangle $ABC$ is a right triangle with right angle at $B$, so we know that $\angle ACB = 90^\circ$. Using the fact that angles in a triangle add up to $180^\circ$, we can write:

$\angle PAB + \angle ABC + \angle ACB = 180^\circ$

$x + 90^\circ + (Mx + N)^\circ = 180^\circ$

Simplifying this expression gives:

$(M+1)x + N + 90^\circ = 180^\circ$

$(M+1)x = 90^\circ - N$

At this point, we still have two unknowns: $M$ and $N$. But the problem tells us that $M = 1$, so substituting this in gives:

$(1+1)x = 90^\circ - N$

$2x = 90^\circ - N$

$N + 2x = 90^\circ$

Finally, we can see that $M+N = 1+N$, and from the previous equation we can see that $M+N = 90^\circ - 2x$. Therefore, we just need to find $x$ to solve the problem.

Remember, even powers of $-1$ equal $1$, and odd powers of $-1$ equal $-1$.  Therefore, $x + x^2 = -1 + (-1)^2 = -1 + 1 = 0$.  The next pair cancels out in the same way: $x^3 + x^4 = (-1)^3 + (-1)^4 = -1 + 1 = 0$.  Now, it is easy to see that the pattern continues for every pair of powers, all the way up to $x^{2009} + x^{2010}$.  Notice that $x^{2011}$ is the only power that hasn't been canceled out.  Therefore, the answer is $(-1)^{2011} = \boxed{-1}.$

We have A geometric series which can be expressed as a fraction with the formula:

$$1+x+x^2 + ... + x^{n} = \frac{1 - x^{n+1}}{1-x}$$

$$x + x^2 + x^3 + \cdots + x^{2010} + x^{2011} = \frac{x-x^{2012}}{1-x}.$$

We get \begin{align*}182+3\cdot 7-64\div 2+27\div 3&=182+21-32+9.\end{align*}Now, we write this as the sum of four numbers so that we can use the commutative and associative properties of addition to make the arithmetic easier. Sure! Let's start by simplifying the left side of the equation:

$3p - 2(p-4) = 7p + 6$

$3p - 2p + 8 = 7p + 6$ (distribute the negative sign)

$p + 8 = 7p + 6$ (combine like terms)

Next, we want to isolate the variable, $p$, on one side of the equation. Let's start by subtracting $p$ from both sides:

$p - p + 8 = 7p - p + 6$

$8 = 6p + 6$

Now, we can isolate $p$ by subtracting 6 from both sides and then dividing by 6:

$8 - 6 = 6p - 6$

$2 = 6p/6 - 6/6$

$2 = p - 1$

$p = 3$

So the solution to the equation is $p=3$.

Convert both decimals into fractions. \begin{align*}
x&=.\overline{2} \\
\Rightarrow 10x&=2.\overline{2} \\
\Rightarrow 9x&=2 \\
\Rightarrow x &= \frac{2}{9}.
\end{align*}Likewise, $.\overline{6}=\frac{6}{9}$. Adding the two fractions yields $\frac{2}{9} + \frac{6}{9}=\frac{8}{9}$. The reciprocal of this is $\frac{1}{\frac{8}{9}}=\frac{9}{8}$. To convert this to a decimal, we need to multiply the numerator and denominator by 125. Yes, of course! Let's solve it step by step:

1. Firstly, remember the ratio for the three friends: 4:2:1 means that for every 4 parts Carolyn gets, Julie gets 2 parts and Roberta gets 1 part.

2. Next, we need to add up all the parts in the ratio to find the total number of parts: 4 + 2 + 1 = 7

3. Now we need to figure out how much each part is worth. We do this by dividing the total amount of money they have by the total number of parts: $77 ÷ 7$ = $11

4. So we know each part is worth $11. Now we can figure out how much Carolyn gets by multiplying her number of parts (4) by the value of each part ($11): 4 x 11 = $44

Extracting Answer from: 
If we can express this number as a single power of 10, then we can directly find the number of zeroes at the end of the numbers. Recall that $10^n$ has $n$ zeroes at the end of it. We must start with parentheses first. Recall that $\left( a^m \right) ^n = a^{mn}$. Because of this, we can rewrite the last term as $10^{15 \cdot 4}=10^{60}$. Finally, recall the rules of division and multiplication of exponents: $a^m \cdot a^n = a^{m+n}$ and $a^m \div a^n = a^{m-n}$. Using these we can carry out the multiplication and division from left to right to get \begin{align*}
(10^5 \cdot 10^{77} \div 10^{15}) \div \left(10^{15}\right)^4 &= (10^5 \cdot 10^{77} \div 10^{15}) \div 10^{60} \\
&=(10^{5+77} \div 10^{15}) \div 10^{60} \\
&=(10^{82} \div 10^{15} )\div 10^{60} \\
&=10^{82-15} \div 10^{60} \\
&=10^{67} \div 10^{60} \\
&=10^{67-60} \\
&=10^7.
\end{align*}Because the exponent of the number 10 is 7, this number has $\boxed{7}$ zeroes at the end.

Extracting Answer from: 
Sure, let's break this problem down step by step.

First, we know that $97$ is the largest prime less than $100$, so we don't need to worry about any primes larger than that.

Next, we need to find the largest prime factor of $97!$. To do that, we need to break down $97!$ into its prime factors.

We can start by dividing $97!$ by the largest prime less than or equal to $97$, which is $97$ itself. We know that $97$ must divide evenly into $97!$, so we get:

$$\frac{97!}{97} = 96!$$

Now we can repeat this process with the next largest prime less than or equal to $96$, which is $89$:

$$\frac{96!}{89} = 92!$$

And we can keep going until we reach $2$, which is the smallest prime less than or equal to $97$:

$$\frac{2!}{2} = 1$$

Now we need to find the largest prime factor of $92!$. We can repeat the process above:

$$\frac{92!}{89} = 88!$$
$$\frac{88!}{83} = 84!$$
$$\frac{84!}{79} = 80!$$
$$\frac{80!}{73} = 76!$$
$$\frac{76!}{71} = 72!$$
$$\frac{72!}{67} = 68!$$
$$\frac{68!}{61} = 64!$$
$$\frac{64!}{59} = 60!$$
$$\frac{60!}{53} = 56!$$
$$\frac{56!}{47} = 52!$$
$$\frac{52!}{43} = 48!$$
$$\frac{48!}{41} = 44!$$
$$\frac{44!}{37} = 40!$$
$$\frac{40!}{31} = 36!$$
$$\frac{36!}{29} = 32!$$
$$\frac{32!}{23} = 28!$$
$$\frac{28!}{19} = 24!$$
$$\frac{24!}{17} = 20!$$
$$\frac{20!}{13} = 16!$$
$$\frac{16!}{11} = 12!$$
$$\frac{12!}{7} = 10!$$
$$\frac{10!}{5} = 8!$$
$$\frac{8!}{3} = 2^6\cdot5\cdot7$$

So we can see that the largest prime factor of $97!$ is $71$.

Remembering that "of" means "times," the number of aliens with 3 eyes is $\frac{17}{40} \cdot 160$.  This equals $\frac{17 \cdot 160}{40}$, which can be rewritten as $17 \cdot \frac{160}{40}$.  Because $160$ divided by $40$ equals $4$, the expression above is the same as $17 \cdot 4$, which equals $\boxed{68}$.

Extracting Answer from: 
To solve this problem, we need to multiply the total number of aliens by the fraction that had 3 eyes. 

$\frac{17}{40} \times 160$ 

We can simplify the fraction by dividing both the numerator and denominator by 8: 

$\frac{17}{40} = \frac{17 \div 8}{40 \div 8} = \frac{2.125}{5}$ 

Now we can multiply: 

$\frac{2.125}{5} \times 160 = \frac{2.125 \times 160}{5} = 85$ 

So there were 85 aliens with 3 eyes on Planet Q.

Sure, here's how to solve the problem:

The circumference of a circle is given by the formula $C = 2\pi r$, where $r$ is the radius of the circle. So the circumference of the circle with radius $1.125$ is $C_1 = 2\pi(1.125)$.

The circumference of a circle is also related to its diameter by the formula $C = \pi d$, where $d$ is the diameter of the circle. So the circumference of the circle with diameter $2.25$ is $C_2 = \pi(2.25)$.

Now we just need to find the ratio of $C_1$ to $C_2$. We can do this by dividing $C_1$ by $C_2$:

$\frac{C_1}{C_2} = \frac{2\pi(1.125)}{\pi(2.25)} = \frac{2}{2} = 1$

So the ratio of the circumference of a circle with radius 1.125 to the circumference of a circle with diameter 2.25 is $1:1$.

First, let's convert the 42 baps into yaps using the given conversion of 5 yaps = 3 baps:

We know that one dragonfruit is $x-4$ dollars.  This means that one rambutan is $(x-4) + 2x = 3x-4$ dollars.  Then, one starfruit is $(3x-4) -5 = 3x-9$ dollars. 6 wallops = 5 ballops and 3 ballops = 11 fallops

Then, let's convert ballops to wallops: 

1 ballop = (6/5) wallops (using the first equation above)

So, 110 fallops is equivalent to 100 wallops.

1. Parentheses (there are none in this expression)
2. Exponents (there is one exponent, $5^2$, which we will simplify first)
3. Multiplication and Division (there is one division, $45 \div (3 \times 5)$, which we will simplify next)
4. Addition and Subtraction (there are two additions and one subtraction, which we will simplify last)

Extracting Answer from: 
Sure, I can help you solve that math problem!

The problem involves permutations, which is when the order matters. In this case, the order in which the books are stacked matters since they are different books.

To solve the problem, we use the formula for permutations of n objects taken r at a time, which is:

P(n,r) = n! / (n - r)!

where n is the total number of objects and r is the number of objects taken at a time.

In this problem, we have 5 books, and we want to stack all of them, so r = 5. Therefore, the formula becomes:

P(5,5) = 5! / (5 - 5)!
P(5,5) = 5! / 0!
P(5,5) = 5 x 4 x 3 x 2 x 1 / 1
P(5,5) = 120

Therefore, there are 120 ways to stack 5 different books on a shelf.

Let me know if you have any other questions!

Sure. Let's solve the problem.

We have to stack the four scoops of ice cream on the cone one on top of another without repeating any combination where chocolate is at the bottom. Let's analyze the situation.

We can ignore the fact that chocolate cannot be at the bottom, and just stack the four scoops in any order. There are 4 scoops to choose from for the bottom, 3 for the next position, 2 for the third position, and 1 for the top position. So, we can stack the 4 scoops in 4 x 3 x 2 x 1 = 24 ways.

However, we have to exclude the cases where chocolate is at the bottom. From the 24 ways, let's count the number of ways that chocolate is at the bottom. There is only 1 way to place chocolate at the bottom, and for the remaining 3 scoops, we can stack them in 3 x 2 x 1 = 6 ways. So, there are 1 x 6 = 6 ways to stack the scoops with chocolate at the bottom.

Therefore, the number of ways to stack the four scoops on the cone, without chocolate at the bottom is 24 - 6 = 18 ways.

I hope that helps!

Suppose I am $y$ years old now.  My brother is 4 times as old as I am, so my brother's age is $4y$. Six years from now, my brother will be $4y+6$ years old and I will be $y+6$ years old. Since my brother will be twice as old as I am at that time, we must have \[4y+6 = 2(y+6).\]Expanding the right side gives $4y + 6 = 2y + 12$. Subtracting $2y$ from both sides gives $2y + 6 = 12$, and subtracting 6 from both sides gives $2y = 6$.  Dividing both sides by 2 gives $y = 3$.  The question asks for the age of my brother now, which is $4y = \boxed{12}$.  (Always make sure you answer the question.)

Let's use algebra to solve this problem.

Let X be my age now.

Then my brother's age now is 4X.

Six years from now, my brother will be twice as old as I will be, which means:

4X + 6 = 2(X + 6)

Simplifying and solving for X, we get:

4X + 6 = 2X + 12
2X = 6
X = 3

So my age now is 3, and my brother's age now is 4X = 4(3) = 12.

Therefore, my brother is currently 12 years old.

Sure, I can help you with that!

To find the area between two concentric circles, we simply subtract the area of the smaller circle from the area of the larger circle. The formula for the area of a circle is $\pi r^2$, where $r$ is the radius. Therefore:

- The area of the larger circle is $\pi (10)^2 = 100\pi$ square inches.
- The area of the smaller circle is $\pi (1)^2 = \pi$ square inches.
- The area between the two circles is the difference: $100\pi - \pi = 99\pi$ square inches.

Therefore, the area outside the smaller region but inside the larger region is $99\pi$ square inches.

Let the width of the rectangle be $w$. Then the length of the rectangle is $2w$. We can apply the Pythagorean Theorem to two sides of this rectangle and get that the length of the diagonal is $5\sqrt{5}=\sqrt{w^2+(2w)^2}=\sqrt{5 w^2}$. We therefore have $5\sqrt{5} = w\sqrt{5}$, which means that $w=5$. This means that the length of the rectangle is 10, so its area is $5\cdot10=\boxed{50}$.

Extracting Answer from: 
Sure, let's solve this problem together!

Let's start by using the Pythagorean theorem to relate the length, width, and diagonal of the rectangle. Let $x$ be the width of the rectangle. Then, the length of the rectangle is $2x$ and the diagonal is $5\sqrt{5}$. We have:

\begin{align*}
x^2 + (2x)^2 &= (5\sqrt{5})^2 \\
5x^2 &= 125 \\
x^2 &= 25 \\
x &= 5
\end{align*}

Therefore, the width of the rectangle is 5 and the length is $2(5) = 10$. The area of the rectangle is the product of the length and the width, so:

\begin{align*}
\text{Area} &= \text{Length} \times \text{Width} \\
&= 10 \times 5 \\
&= \boxed{50}
\end{align*}

So, the area of the rectangle is 50.

Sure, I can explain and solve that problem for you. 

On a 12-hour analog clock, the hour hand completes one full rotation (360 degrees) in 12 hours, or 720 minutes. This means it moves 30 degrees per hour or 0.5 degrees per minute.

The minute hand, on the other hand, completes one full rotation (360 degrees) in 60 minutes, or one hour. This means it moves 6 degrees per minute.

To find the degree measure of the acute angle between the hour hand and the minute hand at 3:20, we need to figure out their positions in degrees and subtract them. 

At 3:20, the hour hand is pointing directly at the 3, which is 1/4 of the way between the 3 and the 4. Since the hour hand moves 0.5 degrees per minute, it has moved 0.5 x 20 = 10 degrees past the 3. So, its position in degrees is 1/4 of 360 (since there are 12 hours in a full rotation) plus 10 times 0.5:

= 90 + 10 x 0.5
= 95 degrees

The minute hand, meanwhile, is pointing directly at the 4, which is 20 minutes past the hour. Since the minute hand moves 6 degrees per minute, it has moved 6 x 20 = 120 degrees past the 12.

So, the acute angle between the hour and minute hand is:

|95 - 120| = 25 degrees

Therefore, the degree measure of the acute angle between the hour hand and the minute hand at 3:20 on a 12-hour analog clock is 25 degrees.

Sure, I can help you with that! 

First, we need to find out how much milk an individual student drinks in a day. To do that, we divide the total number of cartons of milk consumed by the total number of students: 

1500 cartons / 450 students = 3.33 cartons per student per week 

To convert this to a daily quantity, we divide by 5: 

3.33 cartons / 5 days = 0.666 (rounded to 3 decimal places) 

So, each student drinks approximately 0.666 cartons of milk per day. 

Now, we can use this information to estimate how much milk the seniors will drink each school day. Since there are 600 seniors, their total daily milk consumption can be calculated as: 

600 students * 0.666 cartons per student per day = 399.6 cartons per day 

Rounded to the nearest whole number, the average number of total cartons of milk the 600 seniors drink each school day is 400 cartons.

There are $12$ inches in a foot, so the length of the rectangular section of floor is $36$ inches and its width is $24$ inches. It would take $36 \div 6 = 6$ tiles to cover the length of the floor and $24 \div 6 = 4$ tiles to cover the width, so a total of $6 \times 4 = \boxed{24}$ tiles are needed to cover the whole rectangular section of the floor.

Hi there! 
To solve this problem, we need to first convert both measurements, 3 feet and 2 feet, into inches since the measurements of the tiles are given in inches. 

To convert feet to inches, we need to multiply the measurement by 12 (since there are 12 inches in every foot).

So, 3 feet x 12 = 36 inches and 2 feet x 12 = 24 inches.

Now we know that we need to cover a rectangular section of floor that is 36 inches by 24 inches. 

To determine how many 6-inch by 6-inch square tiles we would need, we will first need to find out how many tiles would fit in one row and one column of the rectangular section. 

Since each tile is 6 inches in both length and width, we can divide the length of the rectangular section by the length of the tile to find out how many tiles can fit in one row. 

So, 36 inches ÷ 6 inches = 6 tiles in one row.

Similarly, we can divide the width of the rectangular section by the width of the tile to find out how many tiles can fit in one column.

So, 24 inches ÷ 6 inches = 4 tiles in one column.

Now we have the number of tiles that can fit in one row (6) and one column (4). To find out the total number of tiles needed, we can simply multiply the number of rows by the number of columns. 

So, 6 tiles (one row) x 4 tiles (one column) = 24 tiles needed.

Therefore, we would need 24 six-inch by six-inch tiles to cover the given rectangular section of floor.

We first have to find what fraction of students walk to school. Since the total fraction of students is $\frac{120}{120}$ or 1, we must find:\[\frac{120}{120} - \frac{2}{5} - \frac{5}{12}.\]To solve this expression, we have to get common denominators. In this case, the common denominator is 120.

To get this common denominator for the fraction $\frac{2}{5}$, multiply the numerator and denominator by 24 to get $\frac{48}{120}$.

To get the common denominator for $\frac{5}{12}$, multiply the numerator and denominator by 10 to get $\frac{50}{120}$. So now we have: \[\frac{120}{120} - \frac{48}{120} - \frac{50}{120} = \frac{120 - 48 - 50}{120} = \frac{22}{120}.\]Notice that $\frac{22}{120}$ can be written as $\frac{2\cdot11}{2\cdot60}$, so our final answer is $\boxed{\frac{11}{60}}$.

The sum of the digits of $54,\!321$ is 15, which is divisible by 3.  Therefore, 3 is the smallest proper factor of $54,\!321$.  It follows that the largest proper factor is $54,\!321/3=\boxed{18,\!107}$.  (Note: to see that $n/d$ is the largest proper factor of an integer $n$ whose smallest proper factor is $d$, observe that if $f$ were a proper factor larger than $n/d$, then $n/f$ would be a proper factor smaller than $d$).

It is almost always easier to use fractions than decimals when dividing. So the first task is to convert these repeating decimals to fractions. First, $.0\overline{3}$: \[
10 \cdot .0\overline{3} = .\overline{3} = \frac{1}{3}\\
\Rightarrow .0\overline{3} = \frac{1}{3} \div 10 = \frac{1}{3} \cdot \frac{1}{10} = \frac{1}{30}.
\]Next, $.\overline{03}$: \[
99 \cdot .\overline{03} = (100-1) \cdot .\overline{03} = 3.\overline{03} - .\overline{03} = 3\\
\Rightarrow .\overline{03} = \frac{3}{99} = \frac{3}{3 \cdot 33} = \frac{1}{33}.
\]We now have the tools to make our calculation: \begin{align*}
.0\overline{3} \div .\overline{03} &= \frac{1}{30} \div \frac{1}{33}= \frac{1}{30} \cdot \frac{33}{1}\\
&= \frac{33}{30} = \frac{3 \cdot 11}{3 \cdot 10} = \frac{11}{10}\\
&= \frac{10+1}{10} = \boxed{1\frac{1}{10}}.
\end{align*}

Sure, I'd be happy to help you solve this problem!

To find the class average, we first need to multiply the number of students who achieved each score by the corresponding score. Then we need to add up these products and divide by the total number of students.

So, for this problem:

- 20 students scored 80, so we multiply 20 by 80 to get 1600.
- 8 students scored 90, so we multiply 8 by 90 to get 720.
- 2 students scored 100, so we multiply 2 by 100 to get 200.

Next, we add up these products:

1600 + 720 + 200 = 2520

Finally, we divide this sum by the total number of students (30) to get the class average:

2520 / 30 = 84

Therefore, the class average on this test was 84.

Sure! Let's solve the problem. 

In the diagram, we know that line $l$ is a straight line, meaning that the sum of the angles $x+26^\circ$ and $2x+10^\circ$ must be $180^\circ$. 

So we can set up the equation: 

$$x+26^\circ+2x+10^\circ = 180^\circ$$ 

Simplifying the left side, we get: 

$$3x+36^\circ = 180^\circ$$ 

Subtracting $36^\circ$ from both sides, we get: 

$$3x = 144^\circ$$ 

Dividing both sides by $3$, we get: 

$$x = 48^\circ$$ 

Therefore, the value of $x$ in the diagram is $48^\circ$.

To check whether a number is divisible by 9, we add up its digits. If the sum is divisible by 9, then the original number is divisible by 9.

Sure thing! 

When dividing fractions, we can flip the second fraction (the divisor) and change the operation to multiplication instead of division. 

So, we have: 

$$\frac{25}{4} \div \frac{1}{12} = \frac{25}{4} \times \frac{12}{1}$$ 

Next, we can simplify the fraction by canceling out any common factors between the numerator and the denominator. 

The number 25 and 5 have a common factor of 5. Also, the number 4 and 2 have a common factor of 2. 

So, we have: 

$$\frac{25}{4} \times \frac{12}{1} = \frac{5 \cdot 5}{2 \cdot 1} \times \frac{3 \cdot 2 \cdot 2}{1}$$ 

Now, we can multiply across the numerators and denominators: 

$$\frac{5 \cdot 5}{2 \cdot 1} \times \frac{3 \cdot 2 \cdot 2}{1} = \frac{25 \cdot 12}{2} =\frac{300}{2} = \boxed{150}$$ 

Therefore, $\frac{25}{4}$ divided by $\frac{1}{12}$ is equal to 150.

Sure, I can definitely help you with that! 

To solve this problem, we can use the fact that the perimeter of the octagon is equal to the perimeter of the hexagon. 

First, let's find the perimeter of the hexagon: 

Since all the sides of the hexagon are the same length, we can multiply the length of one side by 6 to find the perimeter. 

Perimeter of hexagon = 16 cm x 6 = 96 cm 

Now we know that the perimeter of the octagon is also 96 cm. 

An octagon has 8 sides, so we can divide the perimeter by 8 to find the length of each side of the octagon: 

Perimeter of octagon = 96 cm 
Length of each side of octagon = Perimeter / number of sides 
Length of each side of octagon = 96 cm / 8 = 12 cm 

Therefore, the length of each side of the octagon is 12 cm.

Sure! To solve this problem, you can use a proportion. The scale tells us that for every 0.5 cm on the map, there is 1 km in real life.

So we can set up the proportion:

0.5 cm / 1 km = 4 cm / x km

where x is the number of kilometers the cities are apart in real life.

To solve for x, we can cross-multiply:

0.5 cm * x km = 4 cm * 1 km

0.5x = 4

x = 8

Therefore, the cities are 8 kilometers apart in real life.
